<p><em>Visit the <a href="//www.highsnobiety.com/2017/02/24/yeezy-boost-350-v2-cream-white-release/" target="_blank">original post</a> to see all 6 images from this gallery.</em></p> <p>Yeezy Mafia has done it again. The YEEZY Boost rumor specialist has just shared what appears to be official adidas images of the YEEZY Boost 350 V2 &#8220;Cream White.&#8221;</p> <p>The site has correctly called a number of popular release dates, and even shared <a href="//www.highsnobiety.com/2017/02/16/yeezy-boost-350-v2-zebra-release-date/" target="_blank">official images</a> of the &#8220;Zebra&#8221; YEEZY weeks before <a href="//www.highsnobiety.com/2017/02/21/adidas-yeezy-boost-350-v2-zebra-store-list/" target="_blank">this weekend&#8217;s drop</a>.</p> <blockquote class="twitter-tweet" data-width="550"><p lang="en" dir="ltr">YEEZY BOOST 350 V2<br/>Cream White / Cream White<br/>April 2017<a href="https://twitter.com/hashtag/MafiaSZN?src=hash">#MafiaSZN</a> RT <a href="https://t.co/N9MCz7aqIx">pic.twitter.com/N9MCz7aqIx</a></p> <p>&mdash; Yeezy Mafia (@theyeezymafia) <a href="https://twitter.com/theyeezymafia/status/835111971590664192">February 24, 2017</a></p> </blockquote> <p><script async src="//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script></p> <p>The “Cream White” colorway sees the redesigned V2 model dressed up in a silky smooth off-white. The images show that the “SPLY-350″ lettering has also been whited out to the point where it&#8217;s almost indistinguishable from the rest of the upper.</p> <p>Yeezy Mafia says the shoe will release in both adult and kid&#8217;s sizes sometime in April. Spy the pics above and stay tuned for more information.</p> <p>In other sneaker news, adidas is re-releasing the Ultra Boost 3.0 “Triple Black” <a href="//www.highsnobiety.com/2017/02/24/adidas-ultra-boost-3-0-triple-black-release/" target="_blank">next week</a>.</p> <p><em>Subscribe to Highsnobiety’s <a href="https://www.messenger.com/t/highsnobietysneakers/" target="_blank">sneaker chatbot</a> on Facebook to receive lightning quick updates on release dates, sneaker street style, shopping tips and more.</em></p> <p> All images and written content is property of the listed RSS FEED if you would like more on this story and images please click the listed feed. <a src='http://up.anv.bz/latest/scripts/anvload.js'></script></div> <p><strong>BRIDGEPORT, Conn. (CBSNewYork) &#8212; </strong>Police have canceled an AMBER Alert for a 6-year-old Bridgeport girl who authorities say was abducted by her father, who is also suspected in a double stabbing.</p> <p>Aylin Sofia Hernandez has been recovered and her father, 39-year-old Oscar Hernandez, is in custody, according to Pennsylvania State Police.</p> <p>The two were found in Pennsylvania, according to police.</p> <div class="embed"> <div class="embed-twitter"> <blockquote class="twitter-tweet" data-width="420"> <p lang="en" dir="ltr">UPDATE: The suspect is in custody and the child has been recovered. <a href="https://t.co/JV4m1AKsFu">https://t.co/JV4m1AKsFu</a></p> <p>&mdash; PA State Police (@PAStatePolice) <a href="https://twitter.com/PAStatePolice/status/835164108177698816">February 24, 2017</a></p> </blockquote> <p><script async src="//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script></div> </div> <p>It all started around 2:45 a.m. when police responded to a home on Greenwood Street in Bridgeport. There, they found two stabbing victims. One of the victims died, but the other is expected to survive.</p> <p>The <a href="https://amber.ny.gov/">alert issued in New York</a> said the suspect abducted the little girl after allegedly committing the homicide.</p> <p>Authorities had been looking for a grey or silver Hyundai Sonata with Connecticut license plate number AG91925.</p> <p>Police said Oscar Hernandez was last seen traveling on Jennings Street in the Bronx. But Pennsylvania State Police say the two were later believed to be in the Altoona, Pennsylvania area.</p> <p><em>Stay with CBSNewYork.com as this story continues to develop.</em></p> <p><img alt="" border="0" src="wp-content/plugins/speed-booster-pack/inc/images/1x1.trans.gif" data-lazy-src="//pixel.wp.com/b.gif?host=newyork.cbslocal.com&#038;blog=14578484&#038;post=1347348&#038;subd=cbsnewyork&#038;ref=&#038;feed=1" width="1" height="1"/><noscript><img alt="" border="0" src="//pixel.wp.com/b.gif?host=newyork.cbslocal.com&#038;blog=14578484&#038;post=1347348&#038;subd=cbsnewyork&#038;ref=&#038;feed=1" width="1" height="1"/></noscript> All images and written content is property of the listed RSS FEED if you would like more on this story and images please click the listed feed. <a href="//newyork.cbslocal.com/feed/" target="_blank">http://newyork.cbslocal.com/feed/</a></p> </div> </article> <article id="post-111733" class="post-111733 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-fashion-music-gate"> <header class="entry-header"> <div class="entry-meta"> <span class="cat-links"><a href="category/fashion-music-gate/" rel="category tag">Fashion &amp; Music Gate</a></span> </div> <h1 class="entry-title"><a href="fashion-music-gate/on-the-rise-23rd-nation-drops-debut-project-fear-the-23rd/" rel="bookmark">On The Rise: 23rd Nation Drops Debut Project, Fear The 23rd</a></h1> <div class="entry-meta"> <span class="entry-date"><a href="fashion-music-gate/on-the-rise-23rd-nation-drops-debut-project-fear-the-23rd/" rel="bookmark"><time class="entry-date" datetime="2017-02-24T16:04:22+00:00">February 24, 2017</time></a></span> <span class="byline"><span class="author vcard"><a class="url fn n" href="author/admin/" rel="author">admin</a></span></span> <span class="comments-link"><a href="fashion-music-gate/on-the-rise-23rd-nation-drops-debut-project-fear-the-23rd/#respond" title="Comment on On The Rise: 23rd Nation Drops Debut Project, Fear The 23rd">Leave a comment</a></span> </div> </header> <div class="entry-content"> <p><span style="font-weight: 400">For years, it seemed like the art of the rap group was dying in music. It seemed as though consumers were more intrigued with solo acts, and groups were forming but crumbling at an alarming rate. Then, you turn on music from a group like <strong>23rd Nation</strong>, and you&#8217;re forced to step back, and as a hip hop enthusiast you step back and think that the art of the rap group is alive, and well. </span></p> <p>23rd Nation, with blends of <strong>Lil Wayne</strong>, <strong>Wu Tang</strong>, <strong>Outkast</strong>, and millennial fire power, delivers a breathtaking body of work on Fear The 23rd.</p> <p>Start to finish listens are a rarity today, even amongst mainstream heavyweights. It&#8217;s usually because of redundancy. If an artists’ track list has 10 songs, if after five songs you&#8217;ve heard the same track five times, then you won&#8217;t want to hear the next five. With 23rd Nation, because of the shock value from track to track, and all of the different sounds, and voice manipulations, running through this eight song track list was actually easy, and boosted its replay value.</p> <p>When Did Fear The 23rd Go Up</p> <p>When you get to “Fire, Fire”, and you swivel your head looking for <strong>Travis Scott</strong> to jump on the track, you know that what these guys have is special, and industry ready, like today. The transition from “Isabella” to “Fire, Fire” was that shock value before mentioned, and was an early indicator that the listener would be able to let the entire project run. Sometimes the first 2-3 tracks of a project can be deceiving, but this didn&#8217;t lend itself for skepticism, but rather provided hope.</p> <p>Fear The 23rd By The Halfway Mark</p> <p>At Halftime, what was the status of the project? Well, “Wind Up” provided lyrical excercise, but in a catchy manner. At times, artist have to compromise one for the other, but on first listen, it seems as though 23rd Nation has that skill down to a science. They have seemingly mastered the art of conveying a message, while keeping the listener engaged, and “Wind Up” at the halfway Mark was a great indication of such. Once again, halftime of a project is the perfect chance to either lose your audience, or keep them along for the home stretch, and 23rd Nation certainly accomplished the latter. “Wind Up” though, could&#8217;ve been placed multiple places on the project, but holding it down at #4 was perfect as a Segway to the backend of the project, it wasn&#8217;t deceptive, and it fit into the overall vision of the project.</p> <p>Fear The 23rd On The Backend</p> <p>How does your project clean up? Artist like <strong>Future</strong>, <strong>Drake</strong>, <strong>Beyonce</strong>, the megastars, they&#8217;ve mastered the art of the album ending. It&#8217;s all so intentional. Seems as though 23rd Nation is from this same creative makeup, but the backend of Fear The 23rd is so carefully composed. The pocket from “23rd Gang” to “Starfall” is masterful, colorful, grimy, lyrical, and compiled of three bangers. Then, “Adanqua” rounds out the project with a soulful, churchy blend, to close out the show, and wrapped up what was a musical experience.</p> <p>Ultra Light Fear The 23rd?</p> <p>This new mix of spiritual, and hip hop has taken the game by storm, led by <strong>Chance The Rapper</strong>, and <strong>Kanye</strong> To The. 23rd Nation has taken its opportunity to shine the light on Fear The 23rd with all its GOD Dream references, and the game should be here for it. This in a sense is taking the ultimate stance, and takes art to a new level. An art that can/will be appreciated for generations to come. “Adanqua” is so raw, and honest, and transparent, and if like myself, you weren&#8217;t familiar with the collective before, then now you know exactly what they stand for, and what their mission is.</p> </div> </article> <article id="post-111747" class="post-111747 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry
